Subject  :-
Problems with dependencyManagement in maven-release-plugin  
Date  :-
Fri, 28 Feb 2014 14:25:09 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi, we are in the following (simplified and inherited) situation:&#010;&#010;* we use git (wth gerrit) as SCM and review system&#010;* we have a parent project, (let's call it com.example:P) with dependency&#010;management and all our internal and external dependencies there (except for&#010;the partent itself)&#010;* let's say we have a 'son' project com.example.test:A without other&#010;dependencies&#010;&#010;P version 1.0.0-SNAPSHOT POM specifies A version as ${project.version}, so&#010;it moves in synchronicity with P&#010;&#010;we want to use maven release plugin to prepare two local changes for its&#010;release. I use shell to illustrate, but the process can equally be done by&#010;hand&#010;&#010;export VERSION=1.0.0&#010;export NEW_VERSION=1.0.1-SNAPSHOT&#010;&#010;# Release the parent with 1.0&#010;mvn -B -Dmaven.repo.local=${LOCAL_REPO} release:clean release:prepare&#010;-DreleaseVersion=${VERSION} -Dtag=P-${VERSION}&#010;-DdevelopmentVersion=${NEW_VERSION} -DpushChanges=false&#010;#... it works&#010;&#010;Now, after I approve the changes in P, I got for A&#010;# clone and cd to A working copy&#010;mvn -B release:clean release:prepare -DreleaseVersion=${VERSION}&#010;-Dtag=${project}-${VERSION} -DdevelopmentVersion=${NEW_VERSION}&#010;-DpushChanges=false -Dproject.rel.com.example.test.P=${VERSION}&#010;-Dproject.dev.com.example.test.P=${NEW_VERSION}&#010;# it does not work&#010;&#010;It refuses to release or to take those values from the parametes. I must do&#010;the release without the -B, using "yes\n\n", "1.0.0", "1.0.1-SNAPSHOT",&#010;"A-1.0.0\n"&#010;&#010;In case there are other dependencies (say, B that depends on P and A), the&#010;plugin will ask for the versions of A, and the will not use them. It looks&#010;like a separate issue, which could be summarized as&#010;* maven-release-plugin does not recompute effective POM after new parent&#010;version is give.&#010;&#010;The first one could be summarized ad:&#010;* maven-release-plugin does not allow to script versions for the parent&#010;element in the POM.&#010;&#010;All tests done with maven 3.0.4 and maven release plugin 2.4.1 and 2.4.2,&#010;just in case.&#010;&#010;Any clue?&#010;&#010;Regards&#010;Santiago&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Releasing clean &quot;company&quot; parent Poms  
Date  :-
Sat, 01 Mar 2014 01:26:21 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;I am currently wondering what the best way would be to deploy a&#010;"company wide" parent POM (with maven release plugin) but have only the&#010;information in the parent POM which is actually about the object model&#010;of the clients (and not the definitions for deploying and testing the&#010;parent).&#010;&#010;I have seen that the ASF and Maven parents have moved some release&#010;related code to a second site-pom. So you dont have the site-specific&#010;definitions cluttering up the parent pom.&#010;&#010;However there is still SCM information and plugins in the parent pom.&#010;&#010;So, basically there are multiple ways, one would be to use deploy-file,&#010;another would be to attach a source file as a deployed artifact. I&#010;wonder if there is a prefered way to do this. Or is there a reason not&#010;to do it.&#010;&#010;My main question is, how the coordinates of the build project and the&#010;build artifacts would overlap?&#010;&#010;So, I was thinking to have a repository like:&#010;&#010;&#010;poms/pom.xml modules=company,... (com.pany.poms:aggregator:1.0)&#010;     company/pom.xml             (com.pany.poms:company-build:1.0)&#010;     company/src/pom/pom.xml     (com.pany.parent:pom:1.0)&#010;&#010;When releasing poms/pom.xml the result would be a released company wide&#010;parent pom which does by itself only contain project/company metadata&#010;and not plugins for itself.&#010;&#010;(I guess the easiest would be to manually deploy a static file, but in&#010;that case I could not automate that with some testing and site&#010;creation).&#010;&#010;I guess this topic is somewhat more relevant since there have been some&#010;discussions about seperating the public visible models from (its own)&#010;build instructions in later POM schema versions.&#010;&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Does what is intended.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; But now, when you open a project in intelliJ13 that uses the&#010;&gt; &gt; android-maven-plugin, IntelliJ declares a problem with the POM that&#010;&gt; &gt; references our MavenLifecycleParticipant.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; What I'd like help with is:&#010;&gt; &gt; 1) Is this a problem with the plugin itself. &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The plugin itself can be found at:&#010;&gt; &gt; https://github.com/jayway/maven-android-plugin&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; A project showing the failure can be found at:&#010;&gt; &gt; in idea.log):&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can recreate the same exception on the command-line using the plugin&#010;&gt; with Maven 3.0.5 (after I removed the 3.1.1 pre-req from the plugin's&#010;&gt; pom.xml)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The issue is that the plugin expects Maven core to supply an&#010;&gt; implementation of org.eclipse.aether.impl.VersionResolver, namely&#010;&gt; DefaultVersionResolver from maven-aether-provider.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; However in Maven 3.0.x the maven-aether-provider module only supplies an&#010;&gt; implementation of org.sonatype.aether.impl.VersionResolver ... which is why&#010;&gt; you see that exception :/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately adding a direct plugin dependency to the&#010;&gt; maven-aether-provider from 3.1.1 won't help because Maven will filter out&#010;&gt; this dependency as being supplied from Maven core&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you want the plugin to work on both Maven 3.0.x and 3.1.x then you'll&#010;&gt; either need to use an API common to both (like the shared&#010;&gt; maven-dependency-tree component) or write two versions of the code that&#010;&gt; talks to Aether and select the appropriate one at runtime using reflection.&#010;&gt; But if you just want to avoid the exception when Intellij processes the&#010;&gt; pom.xml then you could conceivably provide dummy/stubbed @Component&#010;&gt; implementations of the Eclipse/Aether resolver, with the role set to a&#010;&gt; non-default value such as "dummy" so that it doesn't interfere with the&#010;&gt; default implementation provided in Maven 3.1.1&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Name  :- 
Stuart McCulloch &lt;mccu...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Guice provision error with AbstractMavenLifecycleParticipant  
Date  :-
Sat, 01 Mar 2014 20:23:13 GMT  
contents:- 
On 1 Mar 2014, at 19:12, William Ferguson &lt;william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks for the exceptionally clear explanation Stuart.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I don't think we can just avoid the exception with stubbed implementations&#010;&gt; of the Resolver because the the plugin doesn't use the Resolver directly.&#010;&gt; It asks for an Aether RepositorySystem:&#010;&gt;    @Requirement&#010;&gt;    private RepositorySystem repoSystem;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; which is what instantiates the VersionResolver.&#010;&#010;I don’t think this is an issue, just declaring a dummy component locally using @Component&#010;should satisfy the missing binding that leads to the original exception.&#010;&#010;In other words: at the moment you have a broken dependency chain that stops Guice from creating&#010;an instance of the repository system - if you provide a dummy link in the form of a local&#010;@Component(hint=“dummy") that implements VersionResolver then the chain will be complete&#010;from the perspective of the current plugin and the repository system can be created. Of course&#010;you can’t then do much with it because it would be using the dummy resolver, but it would&#010;avoid the original exception at creation time and allow the IntelliJ pom processing to continue.&#010;Note you may also need to stub out other resolver components required by the repository system.&#010;&#010;Of course as Manfred points out, if IntelliJ updated their bundled version of Maven to 3.1.x&#010;or later then that would also solve the problem and doesn’t require any plugin changes.&#010;&#010;&gt; I'll have another look at maven-dependency-tree but I didn't see a clear&#010;&gt; path towards what we wanted.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Could you shed some more light on:&#010;&gt;&gt; Unfortunately adding a direct plugin dependency to the&#010;&gt; maven-aether-provider from 3.1.1 won't help&#010;&gt;&gt; because Maven will filter out this dependency as being supplied from&#010;&gt; Maven core&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; What's doing the filtering and why?&#010;&#010;IIRC this is done in DefaultClassRealmManager from maven-core… the reason it filters out&#010;dependencies/packages explicitly exported by core is to avoid class consistency issues, otherwise&#010;you could end up with the same class being defined twice, once by the core class loader and&#010;once by a plugin’s class loader. Such classes would then be incompatible as they were defined&#010;by different class loaders and couldn’t then be used for sharing data, such as sharing repository&#010;information between core and a plugin.&#010;&#010;&gt; What would be need to make it not filter out a maven-core library that is a&#010;&gt; different version of the running Maven instance?&#010;&#010;You can’t without doing some complicated class loader hacks, this is a fundamental feature&#010;of Maven’s plugin system.&#010;&#010;&gt; William&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On Fri, Feb 28, 2014 at 12:13 PM, Stuart McCulloch &lt;mcculls@gmail.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; On 28 Feb 2014, at 01:17, William Ferguson &lt;william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; As part of the development of the android-maven-plugin we have need to&#010;&gt;&gt; add&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; in an AbstractMavenLifecycleParticipant so that we can modify the compile&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; classpath to add artefacts that are contained within a project's&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; dependencies. Igor provided a lot of the coaching on this.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; The build works fine. Does what is intended.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; But now, when you open a project in intelliJ13 that uses the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; android-maven-plugin, IntelliJ declares a problem with the POM that&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; references our MavenLifecycleParticipant.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; What I'd like help with is:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; 1) Is this a problem with the plugin itself. Ie have we defined something&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; incorrectly.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; 2) Is it just a problem with how IntelliJ is parsing a POM that declares&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; the plugin.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; If it is (1), what do we need to do to fix it?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; However, I suspect it is (2) because similar error messages seem to occur&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; when plugins designed for Maven 3.1 (and the switch to Eclipse Aether&#010;&gt;&gt; from&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Sonatype Aether) are used in a Maven-3.0 environment. I'm thinking that&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; maybe IntelliJ is using a Maven-3.0 core. But I'm really not sure and&#010;&gt;&gt; would&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; love some clarity from those who understand what is going on a bit&#010;&gt;&gt; better.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; And if it is (2) is there anything we or IntelliJ can do to fix it?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; The plugin itself can be found at:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; https://github.com/jayway/maven-android-plugin&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; A project showing the failure can be found at:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; in idea.log):&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; I can recreate the same exception on the command-line using the plugin&#010;&gt;&gt; with Maven 3.0.5 (after I removed the 3.1.1 pre-req from the plugin's&#010;&gt;&gt; pom.xml)&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; The issue is that the plugin expects Maven core to supply an&#010;&gt;&gt; implementation of org.eclipse.aether.impl.VersionResolver, namely&#010;&gt;&gt; DefaultVersionResolver from maven-aether-provider.&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; If you want the plugin to work on both Maven 3.0.x and 3.1.x then you'll&#010;&gt;&gt; either need to use an API common to both (like the shared&#010;&gt;&gt; maven-dependency-tree component) or write two versions of the code that&#010;&gt;&gt; talks to Aether and select the appropriate one at runtime using reflection.&#010;&gt;&gt; But if you just want to avoid the exception when Intellij processes the&#010;&gt;&gt; pom.xml then you could conceivably provide dummy/stubbed @Component&#010;&gt;&gt; implementations of the Eclipse/Aether resolver, with the role set to a&#010;&gt;&gt; non-default value such as "dummy" so that it doesn't interfere with the&#010;&gt;&gt; default implementation provided in Maven 3.1.1&#010;&gt;&gt; contents:- 
Just for anyone coming after me ..&#010;&#010;Ended up rewriting everything that referenced Aether to use dependency-tree&#010;instead. It was definitely the way to go. Made everything much cleaner and&#010;simpler and firewalled up from directly using Maven 3.0 or 3.1 code.&#010;&#010;Thanks for all your help Stuart. It was much appreciated.&#010;&#010;William&#010;&#010;&#010;On Sun, Mar 2, 2014 at 6:23 AM, Stuart McCulloch &lt;mcculls@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; On 1 Mar 2014, at 19:12, William Ferguson &lt;william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks for the exceptionally clear explanation Stuart.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I don't think we can just avoid the exception with stubbed&#010;&gt; implementations&#010;&gt; &gt; of the Resolver because the the plugin doesn't use the Resolver directly.&#010;&gt; &gt; It asks for an Aether RepositorySystem:&#010;&gt; &gt;    @Requirement&#010;&gt; &gt;    private RepositorySystem repoSystem;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; which is what instantiates the VersionResolver.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't think this is an issue, just declaring a dummy component locally&#010;&gt; using @Component should satisfy the missing binding that leads to the&#010;&gt; original exception.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In other words: at the moment you have a broken dependency chain that&#010;&gt; stops Guice from creating an instance of the repository system - if you&#010;&gt; provide a dummy link in the form of a local @Component(hint="dummy") that&#010;&gt; implements VersionResolver then the chain will be complete from the&#010;&gt; perspective of the current plugin and the repository system can be created.&#010;&gt; Of course you can't then do much with it because it would be using the&#010;&gt; dummy resolver, but it would avoid the original exception at creation time&#010;&gt; and allow the IntelliJ pom processing to continue. Note you may also need&#010;&gt; to stub out other resolver components required by the repository system.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Of course as Manfred points out, if IntelliJ updated their bundled version&#010;&gt; of Maven to 3.1.x or later then that would also solve the problem and&#010;&gt; doesn't require any plugin changes.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I'll have another look at maven-dependency-tree but I didn't see a clear&#010;&gt; &gt; path towards what we wanted.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Could you shed some more light on:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Unfortunately adding a direct plugin dependency to the&#010;&gt; &gt; maven-aether-provider from 3.1.1 won't help&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; because Maven will filter out this dependency as being supplied from&#010;&gt; &gt; Maven core&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; What's doing the filtering and why?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; IIRC this is done in DefaultClassRealmManager from maven-core... the reason&#010;&gt; it filters out dependencies/packages explicitly exported by core is to&#010;&gt; avoid class consistency issues, otherwise you could end up with the same&#010;&gt; class being defined twice, once by the core class loader and once by a&#010;&gt; plugin's class loader. Such classes would then be incompatible as they were&#010;&gt; defined by different class loaders and couldn't then be used for sharing&#010;&gt; data, such as sharing repository information between core and a plugin.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; What would be need to make it not filter out a maven-core library that&#010;&gt; is a&#010;&gt; &gt; different version of the running Maven instance?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You can't without doing some complicated class loader hacks, this is a&#010;&gt; fundamental feature of Maven's plugin system.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; William&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On Fri, Feb 28, 2014 at 12:13 PM, Stuart McCulloch &lt;mcculls@gmail.com&#010;&gt; &gt;wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; On 28 Feb 2014, at 01:17, William Ferguson &lt;&#010;&gt; william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; As part of the development of the android-maven-plugin we have need to&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; add&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; in an AbstractMavenLifecycleParticipant so that we can modify the&#010;&gt; compile&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; classpath to add artefacts that are contained within a project's&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; dependencies. &#010;Like so…&#010;&#010;Put the following in your pom:&#010;&#010;    &lt;build&gt;&#010;        &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;javacc-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;version&gt;2.6&lt;/version&gt;&#010;                &lt;executions&gt;&#010;                    &lt;execution&gt;&#010;                        &lt;id&gt;jjtree-javacc&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                        &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                            &lt;goal&gt;jjtree-javacc&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                        &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                            &lt;!-- options for JJTree and JavaCC go here --&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;                &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;       &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;   &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&#010;And your “.jjt” files go into “src/main/jjtree.&#010;&#010;You can see an example in the “river-container-core” module at https://github.com/trasukg/river-container&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;&#010;Greg Trasuk.&#010;Open-Source Stream Lead, Web Age Solutions &#010;http://www.webagesolutions.com/courses/open-source-training&#010;&#010;On Mar 3, 2014, at 1:46 AM, Umashanker, Srividhya &lt;srividhya.umashanker@hp.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I want to compile .jjt files into .java files using maven with javacc/jjtree.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The maven-antrun-plugin wiki http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-antrun-plugin/usage.html&#010;says  :&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Some Ant expressions have their respective counterparts in Maven. Thus, one can simply&#010;invoke the corresponding Maven expression instead of using maven-antrun-plugin to avoid the&#010;unneccessary overhead.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Ant expression&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Plugin&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; JavaCC&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; maven-compiler-plugin&lt;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-compiler-plugin/&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; JJDoc&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; maven-compiler-plugin&lt;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-compiler-plugin/&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; JJTree&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; maven-compiler-plugin&lt;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-compiler-plugin/&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Can someone point me to an example on how to use JJtree with maven-compiler-plugin? &#010;Could not find much details on how to use other compilers.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -Vidhya&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

                       &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                            &lt;goal&gt;jjtree-javacc&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                        &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                            &lt;!-- options for JJTree and JavaCC go here --&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;                &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;       &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;   &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&#010;And your ".jjt" files go into "src/main/jjtree.&#010;&#010;You can see an example in the "river-container-core" module at https://github.com/trasukg/river-container&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;&#010;Greg Trasuk.&#010;Open-Source Stream Lead, Web Age Solutions http://www.webagesolutions.com/courses/open-source-training&#010;&#010;On Mar 3, 2014, at 1:46 AM, Umashanker, Srividhya &lt;srividhya.umashanker@hp.com&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Some Ant expressions have their respective counterparts in Maven. The m-ear-p repackages the WAR,&#010;&gt; so it's entirely the responsibility of the m-ear-p.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I really can't understand maven's logic to create the war (or to copy&#010;&gt; those&#010;&gt; &gt; jars).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The m-ear-p tries to extract all JARs that are also referenced from&#010;&gt; outside the WAR to the EARs lib folder, so they can be reused by other&#010;&gt; modules in the EAR.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Artifacts that are only used by the WAR should remain in the WAR.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Artifacts that are JSF libraries (like RichFaces, OmniFaces, etc.) should&#010;&gt; also stay in the WAR because otherwise JSF won't scan them for&#010;&gt; initialization. See the link above for more details.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; 1) When I run maven only for the WAR project, the WAR has no jars in&#010;&gt; /lib&#010;&gt; &gt; folder&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Yes, but that's something completely different! The WAR will get&#010;&gt; re-packages by the m-ear-p if you configure skinnyWars for the m-ear-p.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; 2) But when I run maven for all the projects (including the EAR) it&#010;&gt; copies&#010;&gt; &gt; those 3 jars in the war file.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; What am I doing wrong? Why is different the WAR created with maven&#010;&gt; inside&#010;&gt; &gt; the WAR project then for all projects (including EAR)? Linux is an example.&#010;&#010;You can go and use WhatsApp without paying them anything to send a&#010;message, their company was valued at $16 billion despite the fact they&#010;are "uncompensated" by their users.&#010;&#010;Typically, mentors are not getting cash paid by the hour, getting some&#010;kind of value in-kind:&#010;&#010;- the mentor has no time or budget to complete some optional piece of&#010;work on their own, like improving their tools, it wouldn't get done&#010;otherwise&#010;&#010;- the student is an extra tester for the project and related tools that&#010;are of interest to the mentor&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Apache Maven Release 2.5 Released  
Date  :-
Wed, 05 Mar 2014 11:44:35 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache&#010;Maven Release Plugin, version 2.5, together with the&#010;maven-release-manager.&#010;&#010;This plugin automates release management.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/maven-release/maven-release-manager/&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-XXX-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-release-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.5&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Release Plugin - Version 2.5&#010;&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MRELEASE-812] - "prepare" does not commit before tagging and&#010;therefore deploys snapshot instead of release&#010;    * [MRELEASE-862] - Upgrade to Apache Maven SCM 1.9&#010;&#010;&#010;Note in particular that MRELEASE-862 fixes the release plugin to work&#010;with git version 1.8 and newer.&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hervé BOUTEMY &lt;herve.bout...@free.fr&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Deploying archetypes  
Date  :-
Thu, 06 Mar 2014 07:19:31 GMT  
contents:- 
befaore deploying, you'll have to package, which usually attaches the artifact &#010;for later automatic deployment by deploy plugin&#010;see http://maven.apache.org/archetype/maven-archetype-plugin/&#010;and the maven-archetype packaging automating it&#010;http://maven.apache.org/archetype/archetype-packaging/&#010;&#010;&#010;but IMHO, trying to both generate an archetype, package it and deploy it from &#010;the example project is a risky process, because your (example project) pom &#010;will mix configuration for archetype generation/deployment with the valuable &#010;configuration you intend to have in the archetype&#010;&#010;you really should use create-from-project once then maintain the generated &#010;archetype project (and in fact the generic example project in &#010;src/main/resources)&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;Le mercredi 5 mars 2014 08:50:00 Jordan Zimmerman a écrit :&#010;&gt; Hello,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I’d like to configure my project to auto-deploy my generated archetype as&#010;&gt; part of the deploy execution. Is there a way to do this? So, to create the&#010;&gt; archetype, I have this:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;             &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-archetype-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;                     &lt;propertyFile&gt;archetype.properties&lt;/propertyFile&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;executions&gt;&#010;&gt;                     &lt;execution&gt;&#010;&gt;                         &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;&gt;                         &lt;goals&gt;&#010;&gt;                             &lt;goal&gt;create-from-project&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;&gt;                         &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;&gt;                     &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&gt;             &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Is there a way to configure the deploy plugin (or some other plugin) to run&#010;&gt; a “deploy” goal on the generated archetype&#010;&gt; (in target/generated-sources/archetype/target)?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thanks!&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -Jordan&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Status of MRELEASE-835?  
Date  :-
Wed, 05 Mar 2014 14:29:45 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;last year in april I added an enhancement request for the release plugin &#010;that allows a user to automatically resolve snapshot dependencies in &#010;release:prepare, i.e. there's no interaction necessary; see MRELEASE-835. &#010;I also added a patch I made using the source code of version 2.4.1 that is &#010;still applicable even the recently released version 2.5.&#010;&#010;Since the issue was added, there has been no activity on it; it also isn't &#010;assigned to someone, and as far as I have seen there have been at least &#010;two similar requests:&#010;* MRELEASE-463 from 2009 (also with a patch provided)&#010;* MRELEASE-854 from last november, marked as duplicate of MRELEASE-463&#010;&#010;I just wanted to know what the actual status is? Is there no need for such &#010;a IMHO usable and CI- and/or build-server friendly feature? Is there &#010;anything missing in the issue/patch/description/...?&#010;At least a comment such as "I'll look into that" would be nice :-)&#010;&#010;&#010;Regards&#010;&#010;Thorsten&#010;

Hi Sascha,&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; [...] &#010;&gt; &gt; I just wanted to know what the actual status is? Is there no need for &#010;such &#010;&gt; &gt; a IMHO usable and CI- and/or build-server friendly feature? Is there &#010;&gt; &gt; anything missing in the issue/patch/description/...?&#010;&gt; &gt; At least a comment such as "I'll look into that" would be nice :-)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; From my POV I can clearly say that this IS something I would like to see&#010;&gt; it in the release plugin :)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; You can "work around" it by having a pre-step in the CI / build-server&#010;&gt; using the http://mojo.codehaus.org/versions-maven-plugin/ plugin&#010;&gt; (versions:use-releases / use-next-releases or use-latest-releases). All&#010;&gt; a bit clumsy, but you can make it work.&#010;&#010;I know, but in that case you won't have the modified poms checked in into &#010;your SCM; you have to add at least another step to check for local &#010;modifications in combination with an optional SCM commit. If your CI / &#010;build server has lots of projects, well, .... :-)&#010;&#010;Apart from that, imagine the following scenario:&#010;&#010;Your pom.xml references a dependency in version, say, 1.2.3-SNAPSHOT. Your &#010;repo contains&#010;- 1.2.3 (release)&#010;- 2.0.0&#010;where 2.0.0 has incompatible changes compared to 1.2.3. With &#010;"versions:use-latest-release", you'll eventually get an unreleasable &#010;artifact because it doesn't compile.&#010;&#010;The feature request in MRELEASE-835 and the provided patch avoids that.&#010;&#010;&#010;Greetings&#010;&#010;Thorsten&#010;

Elliot Metsger &lt;emets...@gmail.com&gt;

Re: Status of MRELEASE-835?  
Date  :-
Thu, 06 Mar 2014 03:11:55 GMT  
contents:- 
I've been using a version of the patch locally, and it's been helpful.&#010;&#010;We have a relatively large project, with multiple modules that can be&#010;versioned independently of each other.  Ultimately, these modules get&#010;packaged into a war at release time.  In order to insure that these modules&#010;use the same version of dependencies, they inherit from a parent pom that&#010;contains a huge &lt;dependencyManagement&gt; element; every &lt;dependency&gt; is&#010;defined there (~90 managed SNAPSHOT deps).&#010;&#010;So when we perform a release, we need to resolve the SNAPSHOT versions in&#010;the parent pom, and that is where the patch attached to MRELEASE-835 is&#010;quite useful.  We can release the parent pom, and resolve the managed&#010;dependencies.&#010;&#010;Things get a little trickier when releasing the descendant modules, because&#010;the check-dependency-snapshots phase will ask you to re-resolve the managed&#010;dependencies from the parent.  So for each sub-module of the parent, you're&#010;potentially answering a lot of versioning prompts - you're re-resolving the&#010;same set of managed dependencies over and over.  Because our sub-modules&#010;can be independently versioned, we have problems using batch mode and&#010;setting the dependencies from system properties.&#010;&#010;Maybe we have a not-ideal project structure, or we're missing some best&#010;practices that we could be applying that could make our release process&#010;easier.  But my immediate thought is that it would be nice for the version&#010;maps for managed dependencies to somehow be made available across Project&#010;releases, maybe in the release descriptor, so that you aren't re-prompted&#010;each time.  It would be really nice if we could define the version maps a&#010;priori, using an easier (?) serialization than a Properties file.  I have a&#010;lot of local hacks that I'd be willing to share, if they'd be considered&#010;useful.&#010;&#010;-Elliot&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Mar 5, 2014 at 4:06 PM, Robert Scholte &lt;rfscholte@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'll look into that.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; For the last couple of releases I've picked up a specific part of the&#010;&gt; plugin and tried to gather all related issues.&#010;&gt; The number of open issues is still huge (and some very old) so it takes&#010;&gt; some time to analyze every issue.&#010;&gt; However, this kind of reminders can help.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Op Wed, 05 Mar 2014 15:29:45 +0100 schreef Thorsten Heit &lt;&#010;&gt; thorsten.heit@vkb.de&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;  Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; last year in april I added an enhancement request for the release plugin&#010;&gt;&gt; that allows a user to automatically resolve snapshot dependencies in&#010;&gt;&gt; release:prepare, i.e. there's no interaction necessary; see MRELEASE-835.&#010;&gt;&gt; I also added a patch I made using the source code of version 2.4.1 that is&#010;&gt;&gt; still applicable even the recently released version 2.5.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Since the issue was added, there has been no activity on it; it also isn't&#010;&gt;&gt; assigned to someone, and as far as I have seen there have been at least&#010;&gt;&gt; two similar requests:&#010;&gt;&gt; * MRELEASE-463 from 2009 (also with a patch provided)&#010;&gt;&gt; * MRELEASE-854 from last november, marked as duplicate of MRELEASE-463&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I just wanted to know what the actual status is? &gt; With maven version 3.2.1, in fact same issue since version 3.1.1, I get&#010;&gt; the exception SCHWERWIEGEND: EJB5070: Exception creating stateless session&#010;&gt; bean : [RequirementBeanSL]&#010;&gt; when building the concerned  module with tests. Changing back to run the&#010;&gt; same tests with maven version 3.0.5, all tests run fine and pass.&#010;&#010;Most likely there are plugin and/or jdk changes that are influencing&#010;the change in results. And not just a change in the Maven version&#010;itself.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; I would very much appreciate any hint on how to work around this problem.&#010;&gt; Of course, I could simple stick to maven version 3.0.5 as this works. But&#010;&gt; in the long run I would prefer to keep pace with the newer versions.&#010;&#010;Do the following:&#010;Go to command line.&#010;Go to your project directory/folder.&#010;Set path to be Maven 3.0.5 and run "mvn -X package &gt; mvn305_out.txt".&#010;Set path to be Maven 3.2.1 and run "mvn -X package &gt; mvn321_out.txt".&#010;Run "diff" or a similar command to compare the output.&#010;&#010;Specifically, look at the plugins listed and try to narrow down what&#010;is different which might cause this. You can "lock down" your plugin&#010;versions with &lt;version&gt;[1.2.3]&lt;/version&gt; and perhaps try using a&#010;plugin that shows up when running 3.0.5 in 3.2.1 and vice-versa to&#010;narrow it down.&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I just had a similar problem.&#010;I used the shade plugin with the following exclusion filter and it worked.&#010;Without the exclusion, I had .RSA and .DSA files in the resulting &#010;assembly and with the exclusions, they were omitted.&#010;&#010;You notice that my filter applies to *:*   You might want to try that to &#010;see if your &lt;artifact&gt; specification is not being interpreted as you wish.&#010;&#010;&#010;                         &lt;filters&gt;&#010;                                 &lt;filter&gt;&#010;&lt;artifact&gt;*:*&lt;/artifact&gt;&#010;                                     &lt;excludes&gt;&#010;&lt;exclude&gt;META-INF/*.SF&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;&lt;exclude&gt;META-INF/*.DSA&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;&lt;exclude&gt;META-INF/*.RSA&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;                                     &lt;/excludes&gt;&#010;                                 &lt;/filter&gt;&#010;                             &lt;/filters&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;On 06/03/2014 12:34 PM, Venkata Suresh Kumar Pamidipati wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi Ron,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In the assembly distribution jar, only file present was MANIFEST.MF and there were no&#010;other files. But the jar created from packaging has the .SF and .RSA files which indicates&#010;that exclude configuration did not work. The dependency jar which I have mentioned in pom.xml&#010;is a signed jar and has these .SF and .RSA files.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Suresh&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ----- Original Message -----&#010;&gt; From: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; Sent: Thursday, March 6, 2014 6:50:33 PM GMT +05:30 Chennai, Kolkata, Mumbai, New Delhi&#010;&gt; Subject: Re: Invalid signature file digest for Manifest main attributes&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Look in the jar that the assembly created to see if the excludes&#010;&gt; actually worked.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 06/03/2014 8:09 AM, Martin Gainty wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi Suresh&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;    &#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Your best solution will come from  Oracle Support India&#010;&gt;&gt; They are supposed to know this information and will be able to assist you with your&#010;problem&#010;&gt;&gt; Oracle India Support Line number is +91.22.66796200&#010;&gt;&gt; If  Oracle India is unable to assist you ..we can find a resource on this side of&#010;the planet to help you&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Warm Regards&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Date: Wed, 5 Mar 2014 19:19:44 -0800&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; From: suresh.pamidipati@oracle.com&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Subject: Invalid signature file digest for Manifest main attributes&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I am trying to build our project using maven. contents:- 
Please please please use central.&#010;&#010;Every time you host your own public repo a kitten is horribly mutilated by&#010;the minions of the underworld.&#010;&#010;More seriously if anyone adds your repo they impact their build performance&#010;as they now have another repo to check artifacts against... It's not a big&#010;problem if you only have to add one repo... But the problem grows and next&#010;thing you know your maven build is checking 50 repos for every artifact and&#010;build time is a dog.&#010;&#010;This is why a repo manager is helpful and publishing to central if you can&#010;is the *best* thing to do&#010;&#010;On Wednesday, 5 March 2014, Howard &lt;howard@renci.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks Rafa!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That was in fact the answer.  Well, I did admit it was likely something&#010;&gt; stupid. :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks also to Anders and Joachim for answering.  I will definitely think&#010;&gt; about hosting our jars at maven central.  I didn't realize it was easy. I&#010;&gt; did have a look at managing a repository here at RENCI, but since we hope&#010;&gt; the usefulness of the project outlives it's funding, it would probably make&#010;&gt; more sense for our repo to be off site.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks again&#010;&gt; Howard&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 3/5/14, 3:48 PM, rafal.krupinski@smtsoftware.com&#010;&gt; rafal.krupinski@smtsoftware.com wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  Dnia 5 marzec 2014 o 21:23 Howard &lt;howard@renci.org&gt;      &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;         &lt;groupId&gt;org.renci.databridge-util&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;         &lt;artifactId&gt;databridge-util&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;         &lt;version&gt;1.0-BETA&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;       &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Read your POM, there is no databridge-util in the groupId.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;From the point of view of Git, you're bloating your repo forcing everyone&#010;to download all the JARs when they clone your repo.&#010;&#010;&gt;From the point of view of GitHub, they don't want you to do that and might&#010;very well break it in the future. At least use gh-pages, but that doesn't&#010;solve the Git issue.&#010;&#010;&gt;From the point of view of Maven, repos are a pain for users of your libs,&#010;because each repo will be checked for each dependency. What seemed like a&#010;good idea was badly executed and didn't work well in practice. Please stick&#010;to Central or possibly Bintray.&#010;Le 5 mars 2014 21:24, "Howard" &lt;howard@renci.org&gt; a écrit :&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi all&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I should preface this all by saying that I am not an experienced maven&#010;&gt; user, though I would not describe myself as a complete newbie, so I won't&#010;&gt; be too surprised if I am just doing something stupid here. The&#010;&gt; project name is DataBridge Because this is an National Science Foundation&#010;&gt; funded Open Source project I thought it might make sense to store the jar&#010;&gt; files we produce in a maven repository on GitHub. I found this web page&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://stackoverflow.com/questions/14013644/hosting-a-&#010;&gt; maven-repository-on-github&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; and followed the instructions for one project that produces one jar. &gt; I'm not sure where you mean to check that ojdbc6 is listed as a dependency.&#010;&gt; I am trying to convert the project from using MySql to Oracle,&#010;&gt; so I might not have configured everything correctly.&#010;&#010;Add -X to the call to Maven (mvn -X ...) and pipe the output to a file&#010;(mvn -X ... &gt; out.txt). Then search the file for ojdbc6 to see where&#010;and how the dependency is being brought into your project during the&#010;compile and test steps. Hallo Dave,&#010;&#010;I am not really understand your problem as your report touch multiple&#010;points, so let me do this systematically. Appologies if I state&#010;something obvious:&#010;&#010;a) there is no ojdbc driver in the public maven repositories. The JDBC&#010;driver from oracle is propeitary. So I am not sure where you get that&#010;POM from.&#010;&#010;b) I am not sure how this is related to netbeans, could you make try to&#010;reproduce this with a minimum sample only using maven on the command&#010;line?&#010;&#010;c) if you get "class not found" errors after the download/search in&#010;repository failed that means the pom is missing, if you get the error&#010;after the pom was found it is most likely a configuration issue.&#010;&#010;d) the location where and how you define your dependency in the pom is&#010;responsible where the artifact (if found) is added to the classpath.&#010;There is especially a difference for scope=provided and scope=test&#010;artifaces, but it could also be that the dependency is only defined&#010;local to a specific plugin, and missing to another.&#010;&#010;e) the location of your database is not an issue for the dependency&#010;resolving. You might however (what is typical for ojdbc.jar) define a&#010;dependency with a system path to a locally installed (or copied) oracle&#010;artifact (which could be the XE installation dir).&#010;&#010;f) I am not sore about your sping/jpa test infrastructure, but you&#010;typically dont have to look at the setup there as long as your Pom&#010;fails to get your dependencies.&#010;&#010;Greetings&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;Am Tue, 11 Mar 2014 15:55:59 -0700 schrieb Dave&#010;Kennedy &lt;davek1802@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have tried to simplify the issue by Installing Oracle XE locally to&#010;&gt; eliminate the remote db.&#010;&gt; I am able to connect to the local db with the username and password&#010;&gt; below. Subject  :-
Re: Best way for packaging maven plugin  
Date  :-
Mon, 10 Mar 2014 01:12:52 GMT  
contents:- 
&gt; I have a maven project with many modules, some of them use a maven plugin&#010;&gt; into the goal compile. This plugin is also a module.&#010;&#010;Best practice (IMO &amp; IME) is to have the plugin as its own,&#010;independent project. Then depend on the plugin in your other projects.&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hello,&#010;&#010;we use in a lot of projects special assembly descriptors, which&#010;typically use the following pattern:&#010;&#010;&lt;assembly&#010;...&#010;    &lt;id&gt;distribution&lt;/id&gt;&#010;    &lt;baseDirectory&gt;&lt;/baseDirectory&gt;&#010;    &lt;files&gt;&#010;        &lt;file&gt;&#010;            &lt;outputDirectory&gt;${dist.x}/${dist.base.software.lib}&lt;/outputDirectory&gt;&#010;            &lt;source&gt;${project.build.directory}/x.jar&lt;/source&gt;&#010;        &lt;/file&gt;&#010;    &lt;/files&gt;&#010;&lt;/assembly&gt;&#010;&#010;We are currently cleaning up some POMs and there is a risk that some of&#010;the properties are no longer defined. This produces ZIP files which&#010;have directory or file names in there with unexpanded ${dist*} symbols&#010;(file name not filters).&#010;&#010;Is it possible to make the assembly (archiver?) plugin (and&#010;others) fail in a situation where ${} cannot be interpolated?&#010;&#010;The same would be nice for manifest headers in the maven archiver&#010;(filter in this case)?&#010;&#010;Greetings&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Mon, 10 Mar 2014 20:41:10 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache  &#010;Maven Filtering, version 1.2&#010;&#010;These Plexus components have been built from the filtering process/code in  &#010;Apache Maven Resources Plugin.&#010;The goal is to provide a shared component for all plugins that need to  &#010;filter resources.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-filtering/&#010;&#010;You should add the following dependency to your project:&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.shared&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-filtering&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;1.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Shared Components - Version maven-filtering-1.2&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;     * [MSHARED-161] - DefaultMavenFileFilter.getDefaultFilterWrappers  &#010;loads filters from the current directory instead of using basedir&#010;     * [MSHARED-198] - custom delimiters doesn't work as expected&#010;     * [MSHARED-199] - Filtering doesn't work if 2 delimiters are used on  &#010;the same line, the first one being left open&#010;     * [MSHARED-319] - Filtering throws NPE when using JDK8&#010;&#010;&#010;** New Feature&#010;     * [MSHARED-220] - Apply filtering to filenames&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Max,&#010;&#010;You could create a module (in the same build or outside of it) with pom&#010;packaging and which depends on all the modules of your build. Then when you&#010;list its dependencies, you'll get them all (excluding non-transitive ones&#010;such as optional scope deps).&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Mar 10, 2014 at 4:31 PM, Max Calderoni &lt;max.calderoni@gmail.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; was not able to find a quick way to list a consolidated list of all&#010;&gt; dependencies in your project.&#010;&gt; What i am looking for is something along the lines of dependency:list, or&#010;&gt; dependency:resolve of the maven dependency plugin, but for the entire&#010;&gt; multi-module project.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What i see the maven dependency plugin does is to list by module. Hello Mirko,&#010;&#010;it's an idea. This that you describe in particular i cannot do, because it&#010;will break containment (has implications with site generation, build, etc),&#010;but i had tried a similar hack, by creating a dummy jar project that was&#010;depending on every single module in the entire source tree.&#010;&#010;It almost worked, but not quite, because other than being problematic&#010;remembering to always add every module as a dependency to the dummy module&#010;, both test and not, dependency:list will shrink a dependency to one scope&#010;only. That is, it will not show that dependency A is used as 'compile'&#010;somewhere and somewhere else as 'test', while we want to see that in a&#010;report.&#010;&#010;Seems to me that this problem cannot be resolved with the dependency plugin&#010;alone, because dependencies can only be found by running the entire tree:&#010;the container pom project will run as first in the reactor build order, not&#010;as last.&#010;&#010;Seems more of a problem for a reporting plugin, like for example the Maven&#010;Project Info Reports Plugin.&#010;&#010;I am going to ask a different question based on that, see if i can get an&#010;answer.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;&#010;Max&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Mar 12, 2014 at 10:34 PM, Mirko Friedenhagen &lt;&#010;mfriedenhagen@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello Max,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; what about switching this to  a jar project without sources (maybe a readme&#010;&gt; txt as resource), which is not deployed or installed?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards&#010;&gt; Mirko&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Yes, you're right here that IDE is a good place to check for warnings.&#010;However, we have a requirement for a Maven plugin which accepts a predefined&#010;number of warnings in code (Java/Scala, legacy code which we aren't going to&#010;rewrite anytime soon due to the lack of time) and checks that no more&#010;warnings were introduced since last commit.&#010;The ideas I have in mind:&#010;1) Custom plugin that makes calls to Java/Scala compilers and checks the&#010;code for warnings.&#010;2) Modified maven-compiler-plugin and maven-scala-plugin which can store&#010;warnings and pass them to the custom plugin.&#010;3) Custom plugin parse Maven output log looking for warnings.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Custom-maven-plugin-to-count-compilation-warnings-tp5787921p5788093.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hello,&#010;&#010;Am Tue, 11 Mar 2014 09:20:57 +0000&#010;schrieb "Mao, James(Maode)" &lt;mmao@ebay.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I found that Maven 3.1.1 will try downloading the artifacts in&#010;&gt; parallel.&#010;&gt; This cause the issue, actually the first try already downloaded the&#010;&gt; pom, but Maven still trying other repository in paralle.&#010;&#010;Not sure which issue?&#010;&#010;&gt; In our CI&#010;&gt; server we cannot access repository.jboss.org. that cause the system&#010;&gt; hang until it's timeout.&#010;&#010;You typically add a mirror to external repositories onto your local&#010;repository. Then maven can get those artifacts and you will be able to&#010;archive a local copy to make your build process reproducible.&#010;&#010;&gt; l  Can we configure the threads number for parallel downloading.&#010;&#010;This is a 2.1 feature, it is described in the maven guide:&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/mini/guide-configuring-maven.html&#010;&#010;&gt; l  Why Maven 3.1.1 will try to download artifacts from&#010;&gt; repository.jboss.org, we did not define in our settings.xml and pom.&#010;&#010;You have most likely some POMs in your project from JBoss/Redhat which&#010;have itself defined the JBoss repository. Hi Bernd,&#010;&#010;Thanks for the quick response.&#010;&#010;For example, my project's pom defined only one repository (mycentral), but the dependencies&#010;maybe defined three other repository (jboss/redhat/codehaus)&#010;&#010;In Maven 3.0.5, I guess it download artifacts from 4 repos one by one, so mycentral is the&#010;first one to try, and if it gets artifact from that repo, and it's done. It will not try to&#010;download from the rest repos.&#010;&#010;In Maven 3.1.1, I guess it starts 4 threads to download artifact from 4 repos in parallel,&#010;so here comes the issue. in my server, I cannot access jboss/redhat/codehaus, I can only access&#010;mycentral. So the 1st thread get the artifact, but the other three threads are still trying&#010;to download the artifacts from jboss/redhat/codehaus, which are not accessible. and it's blocked&#010;until timeout, so this really slow down the build.&#010;&#010;I am not sure if what I am saying is correct behavior for Maven 3.1.1.&#010;&#010;If it's correct, seems my options are&#010;1. configure the threads to just 1, so mycental always the first one to try. &#010;2. block all external repositories, just left mycentral.&#010;&#010;Any other suggestions?&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;James&#010;&#010;-----Original Message-----&#010;From: Bernd Eckenfels [mailto:ecki@zusammenkunft.net] &#010;Sent: Wednesday, March 12, 2014 10:43 AM&#010;To: Mao, James(Maode)&#010;Cc: users@maven.apache.org&#010;Subject: Re: Maven 3.1.1 dependency downloading issues&#010;&#010;Hello,&#010;&#010;Am Tue, 11 Mar 2014 09:20:57 +0000&#010;schrieb "Mao, James(Maode)" &lt;mmao@ebay.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I found that Maven 3.1.1 will try downloading the artifacts in &#010;&gt; parallel.&#010;&gt; This cause the issue, actually the first try already downloaded the &#010;&gt; pom, but Maven still trying other repository in paralle.&#010;&#010;Not sure which issue?&#010;&#010;&gt; In our CI&#010;&gt; server we cannot access repository.jboss.org. that cause the system &#010;&gt; hang until it's timeout.&#010;&#010;You typically add a mirror to external repositories onto your local repository. &gt; If it's correct, seems my options are&#010;&gt; 1. configure the threads to just 1, so mycental always the first one to try.&#010;&gt; 2. block all external repositories, just left mycentral.&#010;&#010;Generally speaking, I'd expect you should have a &lt;mirror&gt; for this&#010;"mycentral" defined in settings.xml with a configuration of&#010;&lt;mirrorOf&gt;*&lt;/mirrorOf&gt; which will capture all repo requests, and then&#010;you don't have to worry so much about these other repos finding their&#010;way into your build.&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Mojo's JAXB-2 Maven Plugin 1.6 released  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Mar 2014 09:43:46 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of Mojo's JAXB-2 Maven&#010;Plugin version 1.6.&#010;&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/jaxb2-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;&#010;Significant updates in this relase is the upgrade to JAXB 2.2 and support&#010;for JDK 8. Please also note that the plugin now requires Maven 2.2.1+ and&#010;Java 6+ for execution.&#010;&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin&#010;configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;      &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&#010;      &lt;artifactId&gt;jaxb2-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&#010;      &lt;version&gt;1.6&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-8] - When having multiple executions the jaxb plugin uses same&#010;staleFile for both runs&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-79] - JAXB-2 Maven Plugin don't include the license file&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-80] - Schemagen has namespace prefix problem&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-83] - Provide support for JDK8&#010;&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-61] - Upgrade to JAXB 2.2&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-81] - transformSchema should also replace prefix in "type"&#010;attribute&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-85] - Upgrade dependency to Java 6&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-86] - Upgrade requirement to Maven 2.2.1&#010;&#010;&#010;** Task&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-45] - Add verify scripts for integration tests&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-84] - Convert to Mojo Java 5 annotations&#010;&#010;    * [MJAXB-88] - Random Unit test failure&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;

MDEPLOY-157 deployAtEnd option of maven-deploy-plugin broken after ant-assembly-maven-plugin execution  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Mar 2014 09:45:08 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I recently discovered an issue between the "deployAtEnd" option of "maven-deploy-plugin" and&#010;the execution of my plugin&#010;"ant-assembly-maven-plugin" (based on Aether).&#010;&#010;I first though it had nothing to do with maven-deploy-plugin and revealed a more general issue&#010;in my implementation, so&#010;I posted on Aether mailing list [0] but Benjamin Bentmann answered it could be a bug in the&#010;maven-deploy-plugin&#010;implementation of deployAtEnd option [1]:&#010;&gt;&gt; Aether has nothing to do with the way Maven manages class loaders for plugins, i.e.&#010;you should reach out to the Maven&#010;user list instead.&#010;&gt;&gt; Also, your analysis suggests a bug in the maven-deploy-plugin in that it relies on&#010;the erroneous assumption that a&#010;single class loader is used per plugin through out a multi-module build.&#010;&#010;Here it the issue: the deployAtEndoption doesn't work after building a module involving an&#010;execution of&#010;ant-assembly-maven-pluginbecause a new "Class realm plugin" is then created and its static&#010;fields are reset (in that&#010;case, the org.apache.maven.plugin.deploy.DeployMojo.readyProjectsCounterfield).&#010;&#010;Code from maven-deploy-plugin(readyProjectsCounterrestarted to zero will never equal to reactorProjects.size(),&#010;projectsReadywill be always false):&#010;&#010;    @Parameter( defaultValue = "${reactorProjects}", required = true, readonly = true )&#010;    private List&lt;MavenProject&gt; reactorProjects;&#010;&#010;    private static final AtomicInteger readyProjectsCounter = new AtomicInteger();&#010;&#010;*    *org.apache.maven.plugin.deploy.DeployMojo.execute() {&#010;        boolean projectsReady = readyProjectsCounter.incrementAndGet() == reactorProjects.size();&#010;&#010;&#010;In the following sample case, the ant-assembly-maven-plugin is called by the "nuxeo-distribution-resources"&#010;module.&#010;After that, no deployment will ever happen since the static fields of maven-deploy-plugin&#010;are reset, the counter&#010;"readyProjectsCounter" restarted to zero will never reach the number of "reactorProjects",&#010;"projectsReady" will be&#010;always false:&#010;&#010;$ mvn clean deploy -Pqa -DskipTests -pl nuxeo-functional-tests,nuxeo-launcher,nuxeo-distribution-resources&#010;-nsu -X|grep maven-deploy-plugin&#010;&#010;[DEBUG] Goal: Not sure about your questions, but your finding might explain (or be&#010;related) ti what was found by Karl in this thread&#010;&#010;http://markmail.org/thread/65b7o4so77i7delc&#010;&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;~t~&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Mar 12, 2014 at 10:45 AM, Julien CARSIQUE &lt;jcarsique@nuxeo.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I recently discovered an issue between the "deployAtEnd" option of&#010;&gt; "maven-deploy-plugin" and the execution of my plugin&#010;&gt; "ant-assembly-maven-plugin" (based on Aether).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I first though it had nothing to do with maven-deploy-plugin and revealed&#010;&gt; a more general issue in my implementation, so&#010;&gt; I posted on Aether mailing list [0] but Benjamin Bentmann answered it&#010;&gt; could be a bug in the maven-deploy-plugin&#010;&gt; implementation of deployAtEnd option [1]:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Aether has nothing to do with the way Maven manages class loaders for&#010;&gt; plugins, i.e. you should reach out to the Maven&#010;&gt; user list instead.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Also, your analysis suggests a bug in the maven-deploy-plugin in that&#010;&gt; it relies on the erroneous assumption that a&#010;&gt; single class loader is used per plugin through out a multi-module build.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Here it the issue: the deployAtEndoption doesn't work after building a&#010;&gt; module involving an execution of&#010;&gt; ant-assembly-maven-pluginbecause a new "Class realm plugin" is then&#010;&gt; created and its static fields are reset (in that&#010;&gt; case, the&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugin.deploy.DeployMojo.readyProjectsCounterfield).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Code from maven-deploy-plugin(readyProjectsCounterrestarted to zero will&#010;&gt; never equal to reactorProjects.size(),&#010;&gt; projectsReadywill be always false):&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     @Parameter( defaultValue = "${reactorProjects}", required = true,&#010;&gt; readonly = true )&#010;&gt;     private List&lt;MavenProject&gt; reactorProjects;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     private static final AtomicInteger readyProjectsCounter = new&#010;&gt; AtomicInteger();&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *    *org.apache.maven.plugin.deploy.DeployMojo.execute() {&#010;&gt;         boolean projectsReady = readyProjectsCounter.incrementAndGet() ==&#010;&gt; reactorProjects.size();&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In the following sample case, the ant-assembly-maven-plugin is called by&#010;&gt; the "nuxeo-distribution-resources" module.&#010;&gt; After that, no deployment will ever happen since the static fields of&#010;&gt; maven-deploy-plugin are reset, the counter&#010;&gt; "readyProjectsCounter" restarted to zero will never reach the number of&#010;&gt; "reactorProjects", "projectsReady" will be&#010;&gt; always false:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; $ mvn clean deploy -Pqa -DskipTests -pl&#010;&gt; nuxeo-functional-tests,nuxeo-launcher,nuxeo-distribution-resources -nsu&#010;&gt; Martin Egge &lt;martin.e...@rmcon.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Broken links in surefire-report  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Mar 2014 10:33:32 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I'm using the Maven Surefire Report Plugin to view my jasmine test results (generated with&#010;Jasmine Maven Plugin) as HTML. The generated HTML-Pages look quite good in different browsers&#010;but the links on failed tests don't work at all.&#010;&#010;The XML containing the jasmine results has whitespace and special chars in the names of the&#010;testcases. Theses names are not allowed for HTML-Ids, so the names have to be modified before&#010;using them as ids/targets for anchors/links in the generated HTML.&#010;&#010;This is only done halfway. The anchors have a modified id. Because the SurefireReportGenerator.java&#010;uses sink.anchor() to generate the anchor tags. That function uses DoxiaUtils.encodeId() to&#010;encode any illegal character. But the link targets are wrong. SurefireReportGenerator.java&#010;uses it's own function toHtmlId() which does not implement the same logic as DoxiaUtils.encodeId().&#010;&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Martin&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

IIUC, your project openmeetings depends on red5 libraries.&#010;&#010;About your questions:&#010;&#010;1) Not actually a Maven issue, but you seem to think the way to go it to&#010;build that dependency. As the project is ASLv2, you would far better make&#010;sure/ask it be uploaded to Maven Central. Then just just the &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;in a normal way/&#010;Maven is actually very straightforward if you follow the Maven Way (yeah,&#010;sounds like a sect somehow, you may think ;-)).&#010;&#010;2) Once again, what does contain that tgz? If it contains jars and so on,&#010;then forget about downloading and decompressing it during your buil. Or&#010;you're gonna a world of despair. Just upload those libs under some sensible&#010;coordinates in a corporate (or better, in Maven Central if the project is&#010;OSS), and add the dependency.&#010;&#010;Please ask more questions/give more precisions if you want more precise&#010;help.&#010;&#010;HTH&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-03-12 17:51 GMT+01:00 Maxim Solodovnik &lt;solomax666@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm new to maven and not very familiar with all its plugins.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I need to move project [1] from ant+ivy to maven&#010;&gt; The problems are:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1) this project is build on top of [2] maven project (we need the exact&#010;&gt; structure and all libraries from this project) *[first problem: i don't&#010;&gt; know how to do it]*&#010;&gt;       I did it using ant as follows:&#010;&gt;       a) using SVN download the project sources&#010;&gt;       b) build it using maven&#010;&gt;       c) unpack artifact and use it's structure in my build&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Currently this project was moved to git and I was hoping it will be&#010;&gt; possible to using maven scm:git for this, not sure how :(&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) this project need to download tgz file with required framework, extract&#010;&gt; it somewhere and use extracted file to perform the build *[second problem:&#010;&gt; is this possible?]*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Any help is highly appreciated&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; https://svn.apache.org/viewvc/openmeetings/trunk/singlewebapp/build.xml?view=markup&#010;&gt; [2] https://github.com/Red5/red5-server&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; WBR&#010;&gt; Maxim aka solomax&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Baptiste &lt;Batmat&gt; MATHUS - http://batmat.net&#010;&gt; Sauvez un arbre,&#010;&gt; Mangez un castor ! nbsp;!&#010;&#010;

IMHO, Maven is a software build tool and trying to make it a &#010;installation tool is much too hard.&#010;&#010;You might find that your life will be a lot easier with IzPack as the &#010;tool to create your installer.&#010;It will allow you to package up your maven artifacts with other &#010;resources into different OS-specific installers that can be distributed &#010;easily.&#010;It supports install time execution of your procedures so that you can &#010;start RED-5 or execute the flex processes required to build and install &#010;the Flash assets.&#010;&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;On 13/03/2014 4:51 AM, Maxim Solodovnik wrote:&#010;&gt; Hello Baptiste,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for your quick reply!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Red5-server is "custom tomcat" (zip/tgz with scripts, libraries, configs&#010;&gt; etc.).&#010;&gt; We need to pack it in our distribution, not sure if it can be done "Maven&#010;&gt; way" :(&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) tgz contains flex based Flash compiler with all necessary libraries and&#010;&gt; binaries necessary to build Flash part of our application.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Thu, Mar 13, 2014 at 5:15 AM, Baptiste Mathus &lt;ml@batmat.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; IIUC, your project openmeetings depends on red5 libraries.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; About your questions:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1) Not actually a Maven issue, but you seem to think the way to go it to&#010;&gt;&gt; build that dependency. As the project is ASLv2, you would far better make&#010;&gt;&gt; sure/ask it be uploaded to Maven Central. Then just just the &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; in a normal way/&#010;&gt;&gt; Maven is actually very straightforward if you follow the Maven Way (yeah,&#010;&gt;&gt; sounds like a sect somehow, you may think ;-)).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 2) Once again, what does contain that tgz? If it contains jars and so on,&#010;&gt;&gt; then forget about downloading and decompressing it during your buil. Or&#010;&gt;&gt; you're gonna a world of despair. Re: Help with converting existing ant build to maven is required  
Date  :-
Thu, 13 Mar 2014 13:58:01 GMT  
contents:- 
Well, though I agree Maven isn't designed to be an end-user tool, using it&#010;to build the end-user distribution is actually totally supported.&#010;IMO, if what you're trying to do is building your product from some sources&#010;and binaries, then Maven can obviously do it.&#010;&#010;If what you need for production is an installer, then creating an installer&#010;using izpack is indeed a good idea, but you would just build that installer&#010;during your Maven build (http://izpack.codehaus.org/izpack-maven-plugin/e.g.).&#010;&#010;You seem to actually have two kind of phases:&#010;* the first one, typically compile and package your sources using binaries&#010;coming from a repo manager (be it a corporately managed one, or directly&#010;from Central)&#010;* the second one, creating the end-user distribution, is typically done&#010;with Maven using maven-assembly-plugin.&#010;&#010;Don't hesitate to ask questions, because I don't think we've gone so far&#010;until now to understand your building steps.&#010;&#010;Cheers&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-03-13 14:24 GMT+01:00 Maxim Solodovnik &lt;solomax666@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks Ron,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'll take a look at it, but I'm afraid distribute application in "partially&#010;&gt; compiled state" is not an option.&#010;&gt; Currently it works out of the box and this is the requirement.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Good approach.&#010;Ron&#010;On 13/03/2014 9:58 AM, Baptiste Mathus wrote:&#010;&gt; Well, though I agree Maven isn't designed to be an end-user tool, using it&#010;&gt; to build the end-user distribution is actually totally supported.&#010;&gt; IMO, if what you're trying to do is building your product from some sources&#010;&gt; and binaries, then Maven can obviously do it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If what you need for production is an installer, then creating an installer&#010;&gt; using izpack is indeed a good idea, but you would just build that installer&#010;&gt; during your Maven build (http://izpack.codehaus.org/izpack-maven-plugin/e.g.).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You seem to actually have two kind of phases:&#010;&gt; * the first one, typically compile and package your sources using binaries&#010;&gt; coming from a repo manager (be it a corporately managed one, or directly&#010;&gt; from Central)&#010;&gt; * the second one, creating the end-user distribution, is typically done&#010;&gt; with Maven using maven-assembly-plugin.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Don't hesitate to ask questions, because I don't think we've gone so far&#010;&gt; until now to understand your building steps.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You can distribute it in any state that you want.&#010;I was just pointing out that if you need to do something with the tgz &#010;file at the destination, you can.&#010;If it is ready to be used as a tgz, then you don't need to do anything.&#010;&#010;My point is that trying to make Maven build installation packages can be &#010;more trouble than it is worth and one way around this is to use Maven to &#010;do the building of the artifacts and use an install builder to make the &#010;final package that you send t the deploy stage.&#010;&#010;iZPack works with Maven so I suggested that one but you can use any of &#010;the other free (or commercial) installers to replace the part of ANT &#010;that assembles the various artifacts and resources into a deployment &#010;package.&#010;&#010;You could stay with that part of your ANT process and use the Maven &#010;ANTRun plugin to initiate the ANT stage.&#010;Not as easy to build as an installer but you already have the script in &#010;your curent set up.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;On 13/03/2014 9:24 AM, Maxim Solodovnik wrote:&#010;&gt; Subject  :-
[Failsafe] How to properly conduct integration tests on executable jar files  
Date  :-
Thu, 13 Mar 2014 02:54:57 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;I've got a module that builds an executable jar file using the Maven&#010;Assembly Plugin. I'm trying to setup an integration test (in the same&#010;module) that runs this executable jar file as a separate process and&#010;interacts with it. To fire up the executable jar file, my integration test&#010;requires the path to the executable jar file.&#010;&#010;I'm trying to achieve this by passing a property to the integration-test&#010;via system properties. This makes me feel really really dirty though and it&#010;has issues: although the test runs on the CLI it does not in any IDE&#010;without requiring further configuration (i.e. the property has to be&#010;manually added to a run configuration).&#010;&#010;After googling around a bit and reading the documentation there seems to be&#010;no other option for this scenario. In case I'm overlooking something, I&#010;wanted to ask here if there is a better way to start up this executable jar&#010;file or pass in the needed parameters to do so in the integration test?&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Best Regards,&#010;-- Alex&#010;&#010;

Re: [Failsafe] How to properly conduct integration tests on executable jar files  
Date  :-
Thu, 13 Mar 2014 07:56:14 GMT  
contents:- 
You could use test resource filtering to put the path into a resource file&#010;on the test classpath.&#010;&#010;That way the IDE will pick up the same path.&#010;&#010;On Thursday, 13 March 2014, Alex Karasulu &lt;akarasulu@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've got a module that builds an executable jar file using the Maven&#010;&gt; Assembly Plugin. I'm trying to setup an integration test (in the same&#010;&gt; module) that runs this executable jar file as a separate process and&#010;&gt; interacts with it. To fire up the executable jar file, my integration test&#010;&gt; requires the path to the executable jar file.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm trying to achieve this by passing a property to the integration-test&#010;&gt; via system properties. This makes me feel really really dirty though and it&#010;&gt; has issues: although the test runs on the CLI it does not in any IDE&#010;&gt; without requiring further configuration (i.e. the property has to be&#010;&gt; manually added to a run configuration).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; After googling around a bit and reading the documentation there seems to be&#010;&gt; no other option for this scenario. In case I'm overlooking something, I&#010;&gt; wanted to ask here if there is a better way to start up this executable jar&#010;&gt; file or pass in the needed parameters to do so in the integration test?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Best Regards,&#010;&gt; -- Alex&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Sent from my phone&#010;&#010;

Well with Netbeans you just add the following:&#010;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-surefire-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;version&gt;${surefire.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;                &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;systemPropertyVariables&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;shadedJarPath&gt;${project.build.directory}/${project.artifactId}-${project.version}-shaded.jar&lt;/shadedJarPath&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/systemPropertyVariables&gt;&#010;                &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-failsafe-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;version&gt;${surefire.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;                &lt;executions&gt;&#010;                    &lt;execution&gt;&#010;                        &lt;id&gt;default-integration-test&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                        &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                            &lt;goal&gt;integration-test&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;                &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;                &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;systemPropertyVariables&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;shadedJarPath&gt;${project.build.directory}/${project.artifactId}-${project.version}-shaded.jar&lt;/shadedJarPath&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/systemPropertyVariables&gt;&#010;                &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;and using the Java-task from Ant:&#010;&#010;import org.apache.tools.ant.BuildException;&#010;import org.apache.tools.ant.ExitStatusException;&#010;import org.apache.tools.ant.Project;&#010;import org.apache.tools.ant.taskdefs.Java;&#010;import org.apache.tools.ant.types.Commandline;&#010;&#010;public class ShadedIT {&#010;    @Test&#010;   public void testShaded() throws Exception {&#010;        Java java = new Java();&#010;        java.setProject(new Project());&#010;        java.setFailonerror(true);&#010;        java.setFork(true);&#010;        java.setJar(shadedJar);&#010;        Commandline.Argument arg = java.createArg();&#010;        arg.setFile(csvFile);&#010;        java.execute();&#010;    }&#010;}&#010;&#010;This will be executed by failsafe from the CLI and you may run the&#010;class from Netbeans without any special settings.&#010;Regards Mirko&#010;--&#010;http://illegalstateexception.blogspot.com/&#010;https://github.com/mfriedenhagen/ (http://osrc.dfm.io/mfriedenhagen)&#010;https://bitbucket.org/mfriedenhagen/&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Mar 13, 2014 at 10:50 AM, Adrien Rivard &lt;adrien.rivard@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; If you are using Eclipse you could also pass the system property directly&#010;&gt; to the JRE. ( Windows/Preferences/installed JRE/ edit /default VM arguments)&#010;&gt; It require less work than putting it in all run configuration, but all your&#010;&gt; process will have it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Thu, Mar 13, 2014 at 8:56 AM, Stephen Connolly &lt;&#010;&gt; stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; You could use test resource filtering to put the path into a resource file&#010;&gt;&gt; on the test classpath.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; That way the IDE will pick up the same path.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On Thursday, 13 March 2014, Alex Karasulu &lt;akarasulu@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Hello,&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I've got a module that builds an executable jar file using the Maven&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Assembly Plugin. Hi Kavita,&#010;&#010;I made an external dependency of servlet 2.5 earlier version for the&#010;standard taglib in my app.&#010;This taglib had a transitive dependency on an earlier version of the&#010;servlet api that was messing things up.&#010;By removing this dependency from the path, it worked.&#010;if you do mvn dependency:tree you will see which jar it is that is dragging&#010;in the earlier version of the servlet spec.&#010;&#010;Let me know if this was of any help.&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Shriharsh&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Mar 13, 2014 at 5:13 PM, Kavita [via Maven] &lt;&#010;ml-node+s40175n5788221h23@n5.nabble.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi shriharsh, I am also facing same issue.
